<p><b>Plymouth</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/θ/: 'th' in 'thigh'">θ</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-uk-Plymouth.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c9/En-uk-Plymouth.ogg" class="internal" title="En-uk-Plymouth.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city</a> on the south coast of <a href="/wiki/Devon" title="Devon">Devon</a>, England, about 37 miles (60&#160;km) south-west of <a href="/wiki/Exeter" title="Exeter">Exeter</a> and 190 miles (310&#160;km) west-south-west of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>. It lies between the mouths of the rivers <a href="/wiki/River_Plym" title="River Plym">Plym</a> to the east and <a href="/wiki/River_Tamar" title="River Tamar">Tamar</a> to the west, where they join <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Sound" title="Plymouth Sound">Plymouth Sound</a> to form the boundary with <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>.</p>
<p>Plymouth's early history extends to the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>, when a first settlement emerged at <a href="/wiki/Mount_Batten" title="Mount Batten">Mount Batten</a>. This settlement continued as a trading post for the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, until it was surpassed by the more prosperous village of Sutton founded in the ninth century, now called Plymouth. In 1620, the <a href="/wiki/Pilgrim_Fathers" class="mw-redirect" title="Pilgrim Fathers">Pilgrim Fathers</a> departed Plymouth for the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> and established <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Colony" title="Plymouth Colony">Plymouth Colony</a> – the second English settlement in what is now the United States of America. During the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a>, the town was held by the <a href="/wiki/Roundhead" title="Roundhead">Parliamentarians</a> and was besieged between 1642 and 1646.</p>
<p>Throughout the Industrial Revolution, Plymouth grew as a commercial shipping port, handling imports and passengers from the Americas, and exporting local minerals (<a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lime_(material)" title="Lime (material)">lime</a>, <a href="/wiki/China_clay" class="mw-redirect" title="China clay">china clay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arsenic" title="Arsenic">arsenic</a>). The neighbouring town of Devonport became a strategic Royal Naval shipbuilding and dockyard town. In 1914 three neighbouring independent towns, viz., the <a href="/wiki/County_borough" title="County borough">county borough</a> of Plymouth, the <a href="/wiki/County_borough" title="County borough">county borough</a> of Devonport, and the <a href="/wiki/Urban_district_(Great_Britain_and_Ireland)" title="Urban district (Great Britain and Ireland)">urban district</a> of <a href="/wiki/Stonehouse,_Plymouth" title="Stonehouse, Plymouth">East Stonehouse</a> were merged to form a single County Borough. The combined town took the name of Plymouth which, in 1928, achieved city status. The city's naval importance later led to its being targeted by the German military and partially destroyed by bombing during World War II, an act known as the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Blitz" title="Plymouth Blitz">Plymouth Blitz</a>. After the war the city centre was completely rebuilt and subsequent expansion led to the incorporation of <a href="/wiki/Plympton" title="Plympton">Plympton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plymstock" title="Plymstock">Plymstock</a> along with other outlying suburbs in 1967.</p>
<p>The city is home to 264,200 (mid-2016&#160;est.) people, making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of urban areas in the United Kingdom">30th-most populous built-up area</a> in the United Kingdom and the second-largest city in the South West, after <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>. It is governed locally by <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_City_Council" title="Plymouth City Council">Plymouth City Council</a> and is represented nationally by three <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament (United Kingdom)">MPs</a>. Plymouth's economy remains strongly influenced by shipbuilding and seafaring including ferry links to Brittany (<a href="/wiki/Roscoff" title="Roscoff">Roscoff</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Malo" class="mw-redirect" title="St Malo">St Malo</a>) and Spain (<a href="/wiki/Santander,_Spain" title="Santander, Spain">Santander</a>), but has tended toward a service-based economy since the 1990s. It has the largest operational naval base in Western Europe – <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Devonport" title="HMNB Devonport">HMNB Devonport</a> and is home to <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_University" title="Plymouth University">Plymouth University</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Plymouth" title="History of Plymouth">History of Plymouth</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Plymouth" title="Timeline of Plymouth">Timeline of Plymouth</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Upper_Palaeolithic" class="mw-redirect" title="Upper Palaeolithic">Upper Palaeolithic</a> deposits, including bones of <a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">Homo sapiens</a>, have been found in local caves,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> and artefacts dating from the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> to the Middle <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> have been found at <a href="/wiki/Mount_Batten" title="Mount Batten">Mount Batten</a>, showing that it was one of the main trading ports of the country at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> An unidentified settlement named <i>TAMARI OSTIA</i> (mouth/estuaries of the Tamar) is listed in Ptolemy's <a href="/wiki/Geography_(Ptolemy)" title="Geography (Ptolemy)"><i>Geographia</i></a> and is presumed to be located in the area of the modern city.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>The settlement of <a href="/wiki/Plympton" title="Plympton">Plympton</a>, further up the <a href="/wiki/River_Plym" title="River Plym">River Plym</a> than the current Plymouth, was also an early trading port. As the river silted up in the early 11th century, mariners and merchants were forced to settle downriver at the current day <a href="/wiki/Barbican,_Plymouth" title="Barbican, Plymouth">Barbican</a> near the river mouth.<sup id="cite_ref-early_history_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-early_history-7">[7]</a></sup> At the time this village was called Sutton, meaning <i>south town</i> in <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-early_history_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-early_history-7">[7]</a></sup> The name <i>Plym Mouth</i>, meaning "mouth of the River Plym" was first mentioned in a <a href="/wiki/Pipe_Rolls" class="mw-redirect" title="Pipe Rolls">Pipe Roll</a> of 1211.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The name <i>Plymouth</i> first officially replaced Sutton in a charter of <a href="/wiki/Henry_VI_of_England" title="Henry VI of England">King Henry VI</a> in 1440.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> See <a href="/wiki/Plympton" title="Plympton">Plympton</a> for the derivation of the name <i>Plym</i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_defence_and_Renaissance">Early defence and Renaissance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early defence and Renaissance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prysten_House,_Finewell_Street,_Plymouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_829280.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Prysten_House%2C_Finewell_Street%2C_Plymouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_829280.jpg/220px-Prysten_House%2C_Finewell_Street%2C_Plymouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_829280.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Prysten_House%2C_Finewell_Street%2C_Plymouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_829280.jpg/330px-Prysten_House%2C_Finewell_Street%2C_Plymouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_829280.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Prysten_House%2C_Finewell_Street%2C_Plymouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_829280.jpg/440px-Prysten_House%2C_Finewell_Street%2C_Plymouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_829280.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="481" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prysten_House,_Finewell_Street,_Plymouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_829280.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Prysten_House" title="Prysten House">Prysten House</a>, Finewell Street, 1498, is the oldest surviving house in Plymouth, and built from local Plymouth Limestone and <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a> granite</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Hundred Years' War">Hundred Years' War</a> a French attack (1340) burned a manor house and took some prisoners, but failed to get into the town.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> In 1403 the town was burned by <a href="/wiki/Breton_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Breton people">Breton raiders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> On 12 November 1439, the English Parliament made Plymouth the first town incorporated. In the late fifteenth century, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Castle" title="Plymouth Castle">Plymouth Castle</a>, a "castle quadrate", was constructed close to the area now known as The Barbican; it included four round towers, one at each corner, as featured on the city coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The castle served to protect <a href="/wiki/Sutton_Harbour" title="Sutton Harbour">Sutton Pool</a>, which is where the fleet was based in Plymouth prior to the establishment of <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Devonport" title="HMNB Devonport">Plymouth Dockyard</a>. In 1512 an Act of Parliament was passed for further fortifying Plymouth. A series of fortifications were built, including defensive walls at the entrance to Sutton Pool (across which a chain would be extended in time of danger).<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Defences on <a href="/wiki/St_Nicholas_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="St Nicholas Island">St Nicholas Island</a> also date from this time, and a string of six artillery <a href="/wiki/Blockhouse" title="Blockhouse">blockhouses</a> were built, including one on Fishers Nose at the south-eastern corner of the Hoe.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> This location was further strengthened by the building of a fort (later known as Drake's Fort) in 1596; it was the site of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Citadel,_Plymouth" title="Royal Citadel, Plymouth">Citadel</a>, established in the 1660s (see below).<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plymouth_siege_map_1643.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Plymouth_siege_map_1643.gif/220px-Plymouth_siege_map_1643.gif" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Plymouth_siege_map_1643.gif/330px-Plymouth_siege_map_1643.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Plymouth_siege_map_1643.gif/440px-Plymouth_siege_map_1643.gif 2x" data-file-width="4075" data-file-height="2921" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plymouth_siege_map_1643.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Siege of Plymouth, 1643</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the 16th century, locally produced wool was the major export commodity.<sup id="cite_ref-slaves_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slaves-16">[16]</a></sup> Plymouth was the home port for successful maritime traders, among them <a href="/wiki/Sir_John_Hawkins" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir John Hawkins">Sir John Hawkins</a>, who led England's first foray into the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> as well as Sir <a href="/wiki/Francis_Drake" title="Francis Drake">Francis Drake</a>, Mayor of Plymouth in 1581 and 1593.<sup id="cite_ref-drake_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drake-18">[18]</a></sup> According to legend, Drake insisted on completing his game of bowls on the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Hoe" title="Plymouth Hoe">Hoe</a> before engaging the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Armada" title="Spanish Armada">Spanish Armada</a> in 1588.<sup id="cite_ref-drake_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drake-18">[18]</a></sup> In 1620 the <a href="/wiki/Pilgrim_Fathers" class="mw-redirect" title="Pilgrim Fathers">Pilgrim Fathers</a> set sail for the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> from Plymouth, establishing <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Colony" title="Plymouth Colony">Plymouth Colony</a> – the second English colony in what is now the United States of America.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a> Plymouth sided with the <a href="/wiki/Roundhead" title="Roundhead">Parliamentarians</a> and was besieged for almost four years by the <a href="/wiki/Cavalier" title="Cavalier">Royalists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-civilwar_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-civilwar-20">[20]</a></sup> The last major attack by the Royalists was by Sir <a href="/wiki/Sir_Richard_Grenville,_1st_Baronet" title="Sir Richard Grenville, 1st Baronet">Richard Grenville</a> leading thousands of soldiers towards Plymouth, but they were defeated by the Plymothians at Freedom Fields Park.<sup id="cite_ref-civilwar_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-civilwar-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The civil war ended as a Parliamentary win, but monarchy was restored by <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">King Charles II</a> in 1660, who imprisoned many of the Parliamentary heroes on <a href="/wiki/Drake%27s_Island" title="Drake's Island">Drake's Island</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-civilwar_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-civilwar-20">[20]</a></sup> Construction of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Citadel,_Plymouth" title="Royal Citadel, Plymouth">Royal Citadel</a> began in 1665, after <a href="/wiki/The_Restoration" class="mw-redirect" title="The Restoration">the Restoration</a>; it was armed with cannon facing both out to sea and into the town, rumoured to be a reminder to residents not to oppose <a href="/wiki/The_Crown" title="The Crown">the Crown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-citadel_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citadel-22">[22]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mount_Batten" title="Mount Batten">Mount Batten</a> tower also dates from around this time.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Plymouth_Dock,_naval_power_and_Foulston"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Plymouth_Dock.2C_naval_power_and_Foulston">Plymouth Dock, naval power and Foulston</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Plymouth Dock, naval power and Foulston">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Foulston%27s_Town_Hall,_Column_and_Library_in_Devonport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/John_Foulston%27s_Town_Hall%2C_Column_and_Library_in_Devonport.jpg/220px-John_Foulston%27s_Town_Hall%2C_Column_and_Library_in_Devonport.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/John_Foulston%27s_Town_Hall%2C_Column_and_Library_in_Devonport.jpg/330px-John_Foulston%27s_Town_Hall%2C_Column_and_Library_in_Devonport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/John_Foulston%27s_Town_Hall%2C_Column_and_Library_in_Devonport.jpg/440px-John_Foulston%27s_Town_Hall%2C_Column_and_Library_in_Devonport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="907" data-file-height="577" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Black-eyed_Sue_and_Sweet_Poll_of_Plymouth_taking_leave_of_their_lovers_who_are_going_to_Botany_Bay.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Black-eyed_Sue_and_Sweet_Poll_of_Plymouth_taking_leave_of_their_lovers_who_are_going_to_Botany_Bay.jpeg/220px-Black-eyed_Sue_and_Sweet_Poll_of_Plymouth_taking_leave_of_their_lovers_who_are_going_to_Botany_Bay.jpeg" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Black-eyed_Sue_and_Sweet_Poll_of_Plymouth_taking_leave_of_their_lovers_who_are_going_to_Botany_Bay.jpeg/330px-Black-eyed_Sue_and_Sweet_Poll_of_Plymouth_taking_leave_of_their_lovers_who_are_going_to_Botany_Bay.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Black-eyed_Sue_and_Sweet_Poll_of_Plymouth_taking_leave_of_their_lovers_who_are_going_to_Botany_Bay.jpeg/440px-Black-eyed_Sue_and_Sweet_Poll_of_Plymouth_taking_leave_of_their_lovers_who_are_going_to_Botany_Bay.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="520" data-file-height="405" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Unloading_mail_by_hand_from_the_Sir_Francis_Drake,_March_1926.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Unloading_mail_by_hand_from_the_Sir_Francis_Drake%2C_March_1926.png/220px-Unloading_mail_by_hand_from_the_Sir_Francis_Drake%2C_March_1926.png" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Unloading_mail_by_hand_from_the_Sir_Francis_Drake%2C_March_1926.png/330px-Unloading_mail_by_hand_from_the_Sir_Francis_Drake%2C_March_1926.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Unloading_mail_by_hand_from_the_Sir_Francis_Drake%2C_March_1926.png/440px-Unloading_mail_by_hand_from_the_Sir_Francis_Drake%2C_March_1926.png 2x" data-file-width="611" data-file-height="445" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Unloading_mail_by_hand_from_the_Sir_Francis_Drake,_March_1926.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Unloading mail by hand from the <i>Sir Francis Drake</i> at <a href="/wiki/Millbay_Docks" class="mw-redirect" title="Millbay Docks">Millbay Docks</a>, March 1926</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Throughout the 17th century Plymouth had gradually lost its pre-eminence as a trading port. By the mid-17th century, commodities manufactured elsewhere in England cost too much to transport to Plymouth, and the city had no means of processing sugar or tobacco imports, major products from the colonies. It played a part in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a> during the early 18th century, although it was relatively small.<sup id="cite_ref-slaves_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slaves-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the nearby parish of <a href="/wiki/Stoke_Damerel" class="mw-redirect" title="Stoke Damerel">Stoke Damerel</a> the first dockyard, <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Devonport" title="HMNB Devonport">HMNB Devonport</a>, opened in 1690 on the eastern bank of the <a href="/wiki/River_Tamar" title="River Tamar">River Tamar</a>. Further docks were built here in 1727, 1762 and 1793.<sup id="cite_ref-brief_history_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brief_history-1">[1]</a></sup> The settlement that developed here was called "Dock" or "Plymouth Dock" at the time,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> and a new town, separate from Plymouth, grew up. In 1712 there were 318 men employed and by 1733 the population had grown to 3,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-early_history_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-early_history-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before the latter half of the 18th century, grain, timber and then coal were Plymouth's main imports.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> During this time the real source of wealth was from the neighbouring town of Plymouth Dock (renamed in 1824 to Devonport) and the major employer in the entire region was the dockyard.<sup id="cite_ref-early_history_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-early_history-7">[7]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Three_Towns" title="Three Towns">Three Towns</a></i> conurbation of Plymouth, <a href="/wiki/Stonehouse,_Plymouth" title="Stonehouse, Plymouth">Stonehouse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Devonport,_Devon" class="mw-redirect" title="Devonport, Devon">Devonport</a> enjoyed some prosperity during the late 18th and early 19th century and were enriched by a series of <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">neo-classical</a> urban developments designed by London architect <a href="/wiki/John_Foulston" title="John Foulston">John Foulston</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pdfoul_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pdfoul-26">[26]</a></sup> Foulston was important for both Devonport and Plymouth and was responsible for several grand public buildings, many now destroyed,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> including the Athenaeum, the <a href="/wiki/Theatre_Royal,_Plymouth" title="Theatre Royal, Plymouth">Theatre Royal</a> and Royal Hotel, and much of <a href="/wiki/Union_Street,_Plymouth" title="Union Street, Plymouth">Union Street</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pdfoul_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pdfoul-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Local chemist <a href="/wiki/William_Cookworthy" title="William Cookworthy">William Cookworthy</a> established his short-lived <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Porcelain" class="mw-redirect" title="Plymouth Porcelain">Plymouth Porcelain</a> venture in 1768 to exploit the deposits of <a href="/wiki/China_clay" class="mw-redirect" title="China clay">china clay</a> that he had discovered in Cornwall. He was acquainted with engineer <a href="/wiki/John_Smeaton" title="John Smeaton">John Smeaton</a>, the builder of the third <a href="/wiki/Smeaton%27s_Tower" title="Smeaton's Tower">Eddystone Lighthouse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 1-mile-long (2&#160;km) Breakwater in Plymouth Sound was designed by <a href="/wiki/John_Rennie_the_Elder" title="John Rennie the Elder">John Rennie</a> in order to protect the fleet moving in and out of Devonport; work started in 1812. Numerous technical difficulties and repeated storm damage meant that it was not completed until 1841, twenty years after Rennie's death.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In the 1860s, a ring of <a href="/wiki/Palmerston_forts" class="mw-redirect" title="Palmerston forts">Palmerston forts</a> was constructed around the outskirts of Devonport, to protect the dockyard from attack from any direction.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some of the most significant imports to Plymouth from the Americas and Europe during the latter half of the 19th century included maize, wheat, barley, sugar cane, <a href="/wiki/Guano" title="Guano">guano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sodium_nitrate" title="Sodium nitrate">sodium nitrate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">phosphate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Aside from the dockyard in the town of Devonport, industries in Plymouth such as the gasworks, the railways and tramways, and a number of small chemical works had begun to develop in the 19th century, continuing into the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-legacy_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-legacy-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plan_for_Plymouth_1943"><i>Plan for Plymouth</i> 1943</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Plan for Plymouth 1943">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>, Plymouth was the port of entry for many troops from around the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">Empire</a>. It was developed as a facility for the manufacture of <a href="/wiki/Munitions" class="mw-redirect" title="Munitions">munitions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PD-GreatWar_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PD-GreatWar-33">[33]</a></sup> Although major units of the Royal Navy moved to the safety of <a href="/wiki/Scapa_Flow" title="Scapa Flow">Scapa Flow</a>, Devonport was an important base for escort vessels and repairs. Flying boats operated from Mount Batten.<sup id="cite_ref-PD-GreatWar_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PD-GreatWar-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gateway_to_Royal_William_Victualling_Yard.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Gateway_to_Royal_William_Victualling_Yard.jpg/220px-Gateway_to_Royal_William_Victualling_Yard.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Gateway_to_Royal_William_Victualling_Yard.jpg/330px-Gateway_to_Royal_William_Victualling_Yard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Gateway_to_Royal_William_Victualling_Yard.jpg/440px-Gateway_to_Royal_William_Victualling_Yard.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gateway_to_Royal_William_Victualling_Yard.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Royal_William_Victualling_Yard" title="Royal William Victualling Yard">Royal William Victualling Yard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stonehouse,_Plymouth" title="Stonehouse, Plymouth">Stonehouse</a> by <a href="/wiki/John_Rennie_the_Younger" title="John Rennie the Younger">Sir John Rennie</a>,1825–33.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the Second World War, <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Devonport" title="HMNB Devonport">Devonport</a> was the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Western_Approaches_Command" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Approaches Command">Western Approaches Command</a> until 1941, and <a href="/wiki/Short_Sunderland" title="Short Sunderland">Sunderland</a> flying boats were operated by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Australian_Air_Force" title="Royal Australian Air Force">Royal Australian Air Force</a>. It was an important embarkation point for US troops for <a href="/wiki/D-Day" class="mw-redirect" title="D-Day">D-Day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The city was heavily bombed by the <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a>, in a series of 59 raids known as the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Blitz" title="Plymouth Blitz">Plymouth Blitz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-legacy_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-legacy-32">[32]</a></sup> Although the <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Devonport" title="HMNB Devonport">dockyards</a> were the principal targets, much of the city centre and over 3,700 houses were completely destroyed and more than 1,000 civilians lost their lives. This was largely due to Plymouth's status as a major port.<sup id="cite_ref-gillww2_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gillww2-35">[35]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Church,_Plymouth" title="Charles Church, Plymouth">Charles Church</a> was hit by <a href="/wiki/Incendiary_device" title="Incendiary device">incendiary bombs</a> and partially destroyed in 1941 during the Blitz, but has not been demolished. It has been designated as an official permanent monument to the bombing of Plymouth during World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The redevelopment of the city was planned by <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Abercrombie" title="Patrick Abercrombie">Sir Patrick Abercrombie</a> in his 1943 <i>Plan for Plymouth</i> whilst simultaneously working on the reconstruction plan for London.<sup id="cite_ref-jeremy_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jeremy-37">[37]</a></sup> Between 1951 and 1957 over 1000 homes were completed every year, mostly using innovative prefabricated systems of just three main types/<sup id="cite_ref-EHModern_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EHModern-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 1964 over 20,000 new homes had been built, transforming the dense overcrowded and unsanitary slums of the pre-war city into a low density, dispersed suburbia.<sup id="cite_ref-EHModern_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EHModern-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gillredev_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gillredev-39">[39]</a></sup> Most of the city centre shops had been destroyed and those that remained were cleared to enable a zoned reconstruction according to his plan.<sup id="cite_ref-EHModern_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EHModern-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gillredev_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gillredev-39">[39]</a></sup> In 1962 the <a href="/wiki/Modernist" class="mw-redirect" title="Modernist">modernist</a> high rise of the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Civic_Centre" title="Plymouth Civic Centre">Civic Centre</a> was constructed, an architecturally significant example of mid-twentieth century civic slab-and-tower set piece. The <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_City_Council" title="Plymouth City Council">Plymouth City Council</a> allowed it to fall into disrepair but it was <a href="/wiki/Grade_II_listed" class="mw-redirect" title="Grade II listed">grade II listed</a> in 2010 by <a href="/wiki/English_Heritage" title="English Heritage">English Heritage</a> to prevent its demolition.<sup id="cite_ref-EHModern_38-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EHModern-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Post-war, Devonport Dockyard was kept busy refitting aircraft carriers such as the <a href="/wiki/HMS_Ark_Royal_(R09)" title="HMS Ark Royal (R09)"><i>Ark Royal</i></a> and, later, <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_submarines" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear submarines">nuclear submarines</a>. New light industrial factories were constructed in the newly <a href="/wiki/Zoning" title="Zoning">zoned</a> industrial sector, attracting rapid growth of the urban population. The army had substantially left the city by 1971, after barracks were pulled down in the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-gillredev_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gillredev-39">[39]</a></sup> But the city remains home to the <a href="/wiki/42_Commando" title="42 Commando">42 Commando</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Marines" title="Royal Marines">Royal Marines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gillredev_39-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gillredev-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government_history">Local government history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Local government history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first record of the existence of a settlement at Plymouth was in the <a href="/wiki/Domesday_Book" title="Domesday Book">Domesday Book</a> in 1086 as <i>Sudtone</i>, Saxon for south farm, located at the present-day <a href="/wiki/Barbican,_Plymouth" title="Barbican, Plymouth">Barbican</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-brief_history_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brief_history-1">[1]</a></sup> From Saxon times, it was in the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_(county_subdivision)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hundred (county subdivision)">hundred</a> of <a href="/wiki/Roborough_(hundred)" class="mw-redirect" title="Roborough (hundred)">Roborough</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-genuki-devonhundreds_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-genuki-devonhundreds-41">[41]</a></sup> In 1254 it gained status as a town and in 1439, became the first town in England to be granted a Charter by <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_England" title="Parliament of England">Parliament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-brief_history_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brief_history-1">[1]</a></sup> Between 1439 and 1934, Plymouth had a Mayor.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In 1914 the <a href="/wiki/County_borough" title="County borough">county boroughs</a> of Plymouth and <a href="/wiki/Devonport,_Devon" class="mw-redirect" title="Devonport, Devon">Devonport</a>, and the urban district of <a href="/wiki/Stonehouse,_Plymouth" title="Stonehouse, Plymouth">East Stonehouse</a> merged to form a single county borough of Plymouth.<sup id="cite_ref-early_history_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-early_history-7">[7]</a></sup> Collectively they were referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Three_Towns" title="Three Towns">The Three Towns</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1919 <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Astor" class="mw-redirect" title="Nancy Astor">Nancy Astor</a> was elected the first ever female member of parliament to take office in the British Houses of Parliament for the constituency of <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Sutton" class="mw-redirect" title="Plymouth Sutton">Plymouth Sutton</a>. Taking over office from her husband <a href="/wiki/Waldorf_Astor" class="mw-redirect" title="Waldorf Astor">Waldorf Astor</a>, Lady Astor was a vibrantly active campaigner for her resident constituents. Plymouth was granted <a href="/wiki/City_status_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="City status in the United Kingdom">city status</a> on 18 October 1928.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The city's first Lord Mayor was appointed in 1935 and its boundaries further expanded in 1967 to include the town of <a href="/wiki/Plympton" title="Plympton">Plympton</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Civil_parish" title="Civil parish">parish</a> of <a href="/wiki/Plymstock" title="Plymstock">Plymstock</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-early_history_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-early_history-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1945, Plymouth-born <a href="/wiki/Michael_Foot" title="Michael Foot">Michael Foot</a> was elected Labour MP for the war-torn constituency of Plymouth Devonport and after serving as Secretary of State for Education and responsible for the 1974 <a href="/wiki/Health_and_Safety_at_Work_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Health and Safety at Work Act">Health and Safety at Work Act</a>, went on to become one of the most distinguished leaders of the Labour party.</p>
<p>The 1971 <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1972" title="Local Government Act 1972">Local Government White Paper</a> proposed abolishing county boroughs, which would have left Plymouth, a town of 250,000 people, being administered from a council based at the smaller <a href="/wiki/Exeter" title="Exeter">Exeter</a>, on the other side of the county. This led to Plymouth lobbying for the creation of a Tamarside county, to include Plymouth, <a href="/wiki/Torpoint" title="Torpoint">Torpoint</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saltash" title="Saltash">Saltash</a>, and the rural <a href="/wiki/Hinterland" title="Hinterland">hinterland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The campaign was not successful, and Plymouth ceased to be a county borough on 1 April 1974 with responsibility for education, social services, highways and libraries transferred to <a href="/wiki/Devon#Politics_and_administration" title="Devon">Devon County Council</a>. All powers returned when the city become a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authority</a> on 1 April 1998 under recommendations of the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Commission_for_England_(1992)" title="Local Government Commission for England (1992)">Banham Commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament of the United Kingdom</a>, Plymouth is represented by the three <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_Kingdom_Parliament_constituencies" title="List of United Kingdom Parliament constituencies">constituencies</a> of <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Moor_View_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Plymouth Moor View (UK Parliament constituency)">Plymouth Moor View</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Sutton_and_Devonport_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Plymouth Sutton and Devonport (UK Parliament constituency)">Plymouth Sutton and Devonport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Devon_South_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Devon South West (UK Parliament constituency)">South West Devon</a> and within the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> as <a href="/wiki/South_West_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="South West England (European Parliament constituency)">South West England</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-elected_representatives_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elected_representatives-47">[47]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 general election</a> all three constituencies returned <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> MPs, who were <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Colvile" title="Oliver Colvile">Oliver Colvile</a> (for Sutton and Devonport), <a href="/wiki/Gary_Streeter" title="Gary Streeter">Gary Streeter</a> (for South West Devon) and <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Mercer_(politician)" title="Johnny Mercer (politician)">Johnny Mercer</a> for Moor View.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_Council">City Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: City Council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Council_offices,_Plymouth.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Council_offices%2C_Plymouth.jpg/220px-Council_offices%2C_Plymouth.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Council_offices%2C_Plymouth.jpg/330px-Council_offices%2C_Plymouth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Council_offices%2C_Plymouth.jpg/440px-Council_offices%2C_Plymouth.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Council_offices,_Plymouth.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Civic_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Civic Centre">Civic Centre</a>, 1954–61, symbolic of the Post War 'Heroic Modernism' of the <a href="/wiki/Welfare_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Welfare State">Welfare State</a>; nationally listed in 2009 to prevent its demolition by Plymouth City Councillors</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_City_Council" title="Plymouth City Council">Plymouth City Council</a></div>
<p>The City of Plymouth is divided into 20 <a href="/wiki/Ward_(politics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ward (politics)">wards</a>, 17 of which elect three councillors and the other three electing two councillors, making up a total council of 57.<sup id="cite_ref-wards_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wards-48">[48]</a></sup> Each year a third of the council is up for election for three consecutive years – there are no elections on the following "fourth" year, which is when <a href="/wiki/Devon_County_Council_elections" title="Devon County Council elections">County Council elections</a> take place.<sup id="cite_ref-wards_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wards-48">[48]</a></sup> The total <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/electorate" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:electorate">electorate</a> for Plymouth was 188,924 in April 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_City_Council_election,_2015" title="Plymouth City Council election, 2015">local election of 7 May 2015</a> resulted in a political composition of 28 <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> councillors, 26 <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> and 3 <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Independence_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Independence Party">UKIP</a> resulting in a Labour administration.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Plymouth City Council is formally <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with: <a href="/wiki/Brest,_France" title="Brest, France">Brest</a>, France (1963), <a href="/wiki/Gdynia" title="Gdynia">Gdynia</a>, Poland (1976), <a href="/wiki/Novorossiysk" title="Novorossiysk">Novorossiysk</a>, Russia (1990) <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n" title="San Sebastián">San Sebastián</a>, Spain (1990) and <a href="/wiki/Plymouth,_Massachusetts" title="Plymouth, Massachusetts">Plymouth</a>, United States (2001).<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Plymouth was granted the dignity of <a href="/wiki/Lord_Mayor" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord Mayor">Lord Mayor</a> by King <a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">George V</a> in 1935. The position is elected each year by a group of six councillors.<sup id="cite_ref-lord_mayoralty_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lord_mayoralty-52">[52]</a></sup> It is traditional that the position of the Lord Mayor alternates between the Conservative Party and the Labour Party annually and that the Lord Mayor chooses the Deputy Lord Mayor.<sup id="cite_ref-lord_mayoralty_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lord_mayoralty-52">[52]</a></sup> Conservative councillor Dr John Mahony is the incumbent for 2015–16.<sup id="cite_ref-lordmayor_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lordmayor-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Great_Hall_-_Plymouth_Guildhall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Great_Hall_-_Plymouth_Guildhall.jpg/220px-Great_Hall_-_Plymouth_Guildhall.jpg" width="220" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Great_Hall_-_Plymouth_Guildhall.jpg/330px-Great_Hall_-_Plymouth_Guildhall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Great_Hall_-_Plymouth_Guildhall.jpg/440px-Great_Hall_-_Plymouth_Guildhall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2520" data-file-height="1174" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Great_Hall_-_Plymouth_Guildhall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Great Hall in the Guildhall</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Lord Mayor's official residence is 3 Elliot Terrace, located on <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Hoe" title="Plymouth Hoe">the Hoe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-elliot_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elliot-53">[53]</a></sup> Once a home of <a href="/wiki/Waldorf_Astor,_2nd_Viscount_Astor" title="Waldorf Astor, 2nd Viscount Astor">Waldorf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Astor,_Viscountess_Astor" title="Nancy Astor, Viscountess Astor">Nancy Astor</a>, it was given by Lady Astor to the City of Plymouth as an official residence for future Lord Mayors and is also used today for civic hospitality, as lodgings for visiting dignitaries and High Court judges and it is also available to hire for private events.<sup id="cite_ref-elliot_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elliot-53">[53]</a></sup> The Civic Centre municipal office building in Armada Way became a <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed building</a> in June 2007 because of its quality and period features, but has become the centre of a controversy as the council planned for its demolition estimating that it could cost £40m to refurbish it, resulting in possible job losses.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_places_in_Plymouth" title="List of places in Plymouth">List of places in Plymouth</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plymouth_Sound.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Plymouth_Sound.jpg/220px-Plymouth_Sound.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Plymouth_Sound.jpg/330px-Plymouth_Sound.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Plymouth_Sound.jpg/440px-Plymouth_Sound.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plymouth_Sound.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Northeastward view of <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Sound" title="Plymouth Sound">Plymouth Sound</a> from <a href="/wiki/Mount_Edgcumbe_Country_Park" title="Mount Edgcumbe Country Park">Mount Edgcumbe Country Park</a> in Cornwall, with <a href="/wiki/Drake%27s_Island" title="Drake's Island">Drake's Island</a> (centre) and, behind it from left to right, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Citadel,_Plymouth" title="Royal Citadel, Plymouth">Royal Citadel</a>, the fuel tanks of <a href="/wiki/Cattedown" title="Cattedown">Cattedown</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Batten" title="Mount Batten">Mount Batten</a>; in the background, the hills of <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Plymouth lies between the <a href="/wiki/River_Plym" title="River Plym">River Plym</a> to the east and the <a href="/wiki/River_Tamar" title="River Tamar">River Tamar</a> to the west; both rivers flow into the natural harbour of <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Sound" title="Plymouth Sound">Plymouth Sound</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tamar_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tamar-55">[55]</a></sup> Since 1967, the <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authority</a> of Plymouth has included the, once independent, towns of <a href="/wiki/Plympton" title="Plympton">Plympton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plymstock" title="Plymstock">Plymstock</a> which lie along the east of the River Plym.<sup id="cite_ref-early_history_7-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-early_history-7">[7]</a></sup> The River Tamar forms the county boundary between <a href="/wiki/Devon" title="Devon">Devon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a> and its estuary forms the <a href="/wiki/Hamoaze" title="Hamoaze">Hamoaze</a> on which is sited <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Devonport" title="HMNB Devonport">Devonport Dockyard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tamar_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tamar-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>The River Plym, which flows off <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a> to the north-east, forms a smaller estuary to the east of the city called <a href="/wiki/Cattewater" title="Cattewater">Cattewater</a>. <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Sound" title="Plymouth Sound">Plymouth Sound</a> is protected from the sea by the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Breakwater" title="Plymouth Breakwater">Plymouth Breakwater</a>, in use since 1814.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> In the Sound is <a href="/wiki/Drake%27s_Island" title="Drake's Island">Drake's Island</a> which is seen from <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Hoe" title="Plymouth Hoe">Plymouth Hoe</a>, a flat public area on top of <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> cliffs.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Unitary_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Unitary Authority">Unitary Authority</a> of Plymouth is 79.83 square kilometres (30.82&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-auto_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-3">[3]</a></sup> The topography rises from sea level to a height, at <a href="/wiki/Roborough" title="Roborough">Roborough</a>, of about 509 feet (155&#160;m) above <a href="/wiki/Ordnance_Datum" class="mw-redirect" title="Ordnance Datum">Ordnance Datum</a> (AOD).<sup id="cite_ref-geography_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geography-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>Geologically, Plymouth has a mixture of limestone, Devonian <a href="/wiki/Slate" title="Slate">slate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> and Middle <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">Devonian</a> limestone.<sup id="cite_ref-geology_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geology-59">[59]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Sound,_Shores_and_Cliffs" title="Plymouth Sound, Shores and Cliffs">Plymouth Sound, Shores and Cliffs</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Site_of_Special_Scientific_Interest" title="Site of Special Scientific Interest">Site of Special Scientific Interest</a>, because of its geology.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The bulk of the city is built upon Upper Devonian slates and shales and the headlands at the entrance to Plymouth Sound are formed of Lower Devonian slates, which can withstand the power of the sea.<sup id="cite_ref-geology_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geology-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>A band of Middle Devonian limestone runs west to east from <a href="/wiki/Cremyll" title="Cremyll">Cremyll</a> to <a href="/wiki/Plymstock" title="Plymstock">Plymstock</a> including the Hoe.<sup id="cite_ref-geology_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geology-59">[59]</a></sup> Local limestone may be seen in numerous buildings, walls and pavements throughout Plymouth.<sup id="cite_ref-geology_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geology-59">[59]</a></sup> To the north and north east of the city is the granite mass of Dartmoor; the granite was mined and exported via Plymouth. Rocks brought down the Tamar from Dartmoor include ores containing tin, copper, <a href="/wiki/Tungsten" title="Tungsten">tungsten</a>, lead and other minerals.<sup id="cite_ref-geology_59-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geology-59">[59]</a></sup> There is evidence that the middle Devonian limestone belt at the south edge of Plymouth and in Plymstock was quarried at West Hoe, Cattedown and Radford.<sup id="cite_ref-limestone_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-limestone-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_Form">Urban Form</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Urban Form">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Armada_Way,_Plymouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_83458.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Armada_Way%2C_Plymouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_83458.jpg/220px-Armada_Way%2C_Plymouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_83458.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Armada_Way%2C_Plymouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_83458.jpg/330px-Armada_Way%2C_Plymouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_83458.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Armada_Way%2C_Plymouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_83458.jpg/440px-Armada_Way%2C_Plymouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_83458.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Armada_Way,_Plymouth_-_geograph.org.uk_-_83458.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Armada Way looking north</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 27 April 1944 <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Abercrombie" title="Patrick Abercrombie">Sir Patrick Abercrombie's</a> <i>Plan for Plymouth</i> to rebuild the bomb-damaged city was published; it called for demolition of the few remaining pre-War buildings in the city centre to make way for their replacement with wide, parallel, modern <a href="/wiki/Boulevard" title="Boulevard">boulevards</a> aligned east–west linked by a north–south <a href="/wiki/Avenue_(landscape)" title="Avenue (landscape)">avenue</a> (Armada Way) linking the railway station with the vista of Plymouth Hoe.<sup id="cite_ref-jeremy_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jeremy-37">[37]</a></sup> A peripheral road system connecting the historic Barbican on the east and Union Street to the west determines the principal form of the city centre, even following pedestrianisation of the shopping centre in the late 1980s, and continues to inform the present 'Vision for Plymouth' developed by a team led by Barcelona-based architect <a href="/wiki/David_Mackay_(architect)" title="David Mackay (architect)">David MacKay</a> in 2003 which calls for revivification of the city centre with mixed-use and residential.<sup id="cite_ref-vision_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vision-62">[62]</a></sup> In suburban areas, post-War <a href="/wiki/Prefabricated_home" title="Prefabricated home">prefabs</a> had already begun to appear by 1946, and over 1,000 permanent <a href="/wiki/Council_house" title="Council house">council houses</a> were built each year from 1951–57 according to the <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning#Modern_urban_planning" title="Urban planning">Modernist</a> <a href="/wiki/Zoning" title="Zoning">zoned</a> low-density <a href="/wiki/Garden_city_movement" title="Garden city movement">garden city</a> model advocated by Abercrombie.<sup id="cite_ref-gillredev_39-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gillredev-39">[39]</a></sup> By 1964 over 20,000 new homes had been built, more than 13,500 of them permanent council homes and 853 built by the <a href="/wiki/Admiralty" title="Admiralty">Admiralty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gillredev_39-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gillredev-39">[39]</a></sup> Plymouth is home to 28 parks with an average size of 45,638 square metres (491,240&#160;sq&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-parks_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parks-63">[63]</a></sup> Its largest park is <a href="/wiki/Central_Park,_Plymouth" title="Central Park, Plymouth">Central Park</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> with other sizeable green spaces including <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Park,_Millbridge,_Plymouth" title="Victoria Park, Millbridge, Plymouth">Victoria Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lipson" title="Lipson">Freedom Fields Park</a>, Alexandra Park, <a href="/wiki/Devonport_Park" title="Devonport Park">Devonport Park</a> and the Hoe.<sup id="cite_ref-parks_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parks-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Along with the rest of <a href="/wiki/South_West_England" title="South West England">South West England</a>, Plymouth has a temperate <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a> <i>Cfb</i>) which is generally wetter and milder than the rest of England. This means a wide range of exotic plants can be grown. The annual mean temperature is approximately 11&#160;°C (52&#160;°F). Due to the modifying effect of the sea the seasonal range is less than in most other parts of the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-weather_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather-66">[66]</a></sup> As a result of this summer highs are lower than points further north in the UK; however, the coldest month of February has mean minimum temperatures as mild as between 3 and 4&#160;°C (37 and 39&#160;°F). Snow is rare, not usually equating to more than a few flakes, but there have been exclusions, namely the <a href="/wiki/European_winter_storms_of_2009-10" class="mw-redirect" title="European winter storms of 2009-10">European winter storms of 2009-10</a> which, in early January, covered Plymouth in at least 1 inch (2.5&#160;cm) of snow; more on higher ground. Another period of notable snow occurred from 17–19 December 2010 when up to 8 inches (20&#160;cm) of snow fell through the period – though only 2 inches (5.1&#160;cm) would lie at any one time due to melt. Over the 1961–1990 period, annual snowfall accumulation averaged less than 7&#160;cm (3&#160;in) per year.<sup id="cite_ref-NOAA_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-67">[67]</a></sup> July and August are the warmest months with mean daily maxima over 19&#160;°C (66&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-hku_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hku-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>South West England has a favoured location when the <a href="/wiki/Azores_High" title="Azores High">Azores High</a> pressure area extends north-eastwards towards the UK, particularly in summer. Coastal areas have average annual sunshine totals over 1,600 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-weather_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rainfall tends to be associated with Atlantic <a href="/wiki/Low_pressure_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Low pressure area">depressions</a> or with convection. The Atlantic depressions are more vigorous in autumn and winter and most of the rain which falls in those seasons in the south-west is from this source. Average annual rainfall is around 980 millimetres (39&#160;in). November to March have the highest mean wind speeds, with June to August having the lightest winds. The predominant wind direction is from the south-west.<sup id="cite_ref-weather_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>Typically, the warmest day of the year (1971–2000) will achieve a temperature of 26.6&#160;°C (80&#160;°F),<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> although in June 1976 the temperature reached 31.6&#160;°C (89&#160;°F),<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> the site record. On average, 4.25 days<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> of the year will report a maximum temperature of 25.1&#160;°C (77&#160;°F) or above. During the winter half of the year, the coldest night will typically fall to −4.1&#160;°C (25&#160;°F)<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> although in January 1979 the temperature fell to −8.8&#160;°C (16&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Typically, 18.6 nights<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> of the year will register an air frost.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Plymouth" title="List of schools in Plymouth">List of schools in Plymouth</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Roland_Levinsky_building.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Roland_Levinsky_building.jpg/170px-Roland_Levinsky_building.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Roland_Levinsky_building.jpg/255px-Roland_Levinsky_building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Roland_Levinsky_building.jpg/340px-Roland_Levinsky_building.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1678" data-file-height="2245" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Roland_Levinsky_building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Roland_Levinsky_Building" class="mw-redirect" title="Roland Levinsky Building">Roland Levinsky Building</a> – Faculty of Arts of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Plymouth" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Plymouth">University of Plymouth</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Plymouth" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Plymouth">University of Plymouth</a> enrolls 23,155 total students as of 2015/16 (<a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_the_United_Kingdom_by_enrollment" class="mw-redirect" title="List of universities in the United Kingdom by enrollment">30th largest</a> in the UK out of 166).<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> It also employs 3,000 staff with an annual income of around £160&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-uni_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uni-76">[76]</a></sup> It was founded in 1992 from Polytechnic South West (formerly Plymouth Polytechnic) following the <a href="/wiki/Further_and_Higher_Education_Act_1992" title="Further and Higher Education Act 1992">Further and Higher Education Act 1992</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> It has a wide range of courses including those in marine focused business, marine engineering, marine biology and Earth, ocean and environmental sciences, surf science, shipping and logistics.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The university formed a joint venture with the fellow Devonian <a href="/wiki/University_of_Exeter" title="University of Exeter">University of Exeter</a> in 2000, establishing the <a href="/wiki/Peninsula_College_of_Medicine_and_Dentistry" title="Peninsula College of Medicine and Dentistry">Peninsula College of Medicine and Dentistry</a>. The college is ranked 8th out of 30 universities in the UK in 2011 for medicine.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Its dental school was established in 2006, which also provides free dental care in an attempt to improve access to dental care in the <a href="/wiki/South_West_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="South West of England">South West</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_St_Mark_%26_St_John" title="University of St Mark &amp; St John">University of St Mark &amp; St John</a> (known as "Marjon" or "Marjons") specialises in <a href="/wiki/Teacher_education" title="Teacher education">teacher training</a>, and offers training across the country and abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city is also home to two large colleges. The <a href="/wiki/City_College_Plymouth" title="City College Plymouth">City College Plymouth</a> provides courses from the most basic to <a href="/wiki/Foundation_degree" title="Foundation degree">Foundation degrees</a> for approximately 26,000 students.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_College_of_Art" title="Plymouth College of Art">Plymouth College of Art</a> offers a selection of courses including media. It was started 153 years ago and is now one of only four independent colleges of art and design in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Plymouth also has 71 state primary phase schools, 13 state secondary schools, eight special schools and three selective state grammar schools, <a href="/wiki/Devonport_High_School_for_Girls" title="Devonport High School for Girls">Devonport High School for Girls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Devonport_High_School_for_Boys" title="Devonport High School for Boys">Devonport High School for Boys</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_High_School_for_Girls" title="Plymouth High School for Girls">Plymouth High School for Girls</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> There is also an independent school <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_College" title="Plymouth College">Plymouth College</a>.</p>
<p>The city was also home to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Naval_Engineering_College" title="Royal Naval Engineering College">Royal Naval Engineering College</a>; opened in 1880 in <a href="/wiki/Keyham,_Devon" title="Keyham, Devon">Keyham</a>, it trained engineering students for five years before they completed the remaining two years of the course at Greenwich. The college closed in 1910, but in 1940 a new college opened at <a href="/wiki/Manadon" title="Manadon">Manadon</a>. This was renamed <i>Dockyard Technical College</i> in 1959 before finally closing in 1994; training was transferred to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southampton" title="University of Southampton">University of Southampton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>Plymouth is home to the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Biological_Association_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Marine Biological Association of the United Kingdom">Marine Biological Association of the United Kingdom</a> (MBA) which conducts research in all areas of the marine sciences. The <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Marine_Laboratory" title="Plymouth Marine Laboratory">Plymouth Marine Laboratory</a> is an offshoot of the MBA. Together with the <a href="/wiki/National_Marine_Aquarium,_Plymouth" title="National Marine Aquarium, Plymouth">National Marine Aquarium</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Continuous_Plankton_Recorder" title="Continuous Plankton Recorder">Sir Alister Hardy Foundation for Ocean Sciences</a>, Plymouth University's Marine Institute and the <a href="/wiki/Diving_Diseases_Research_Centre" title="Diving Diseases Research Centre">Diving Diseases Research Centre</a>, these marine-related organisations form the Plymouth Marine Sciences Partnership. The Plymouth Marine Laboratory, which focuses on global issues of <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainability</a>. It monitors the effects of ocean acidity on <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">corals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shellfish" title="Shellfish">shellfish</a> and reports the results to the UK government. It also cultivates <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">algae</a> that could be used to make <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuels</a> or in the treatment of waste water by using technology such as <a href="/wiki/Biochemical_engineering" title="Biochemical engineering">photo-bioreactors</a>. It works alongside the <a href="/wiki/Boots_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Boots Group">Boots Group</a> to investigate the use of algae in skin care protects, taking advantage of the chemicals they contain that adapt to protect themselves from the sun.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>From the 2011 Census, the <a href="/wiki/Office_for_National_Statistics" title="Office for National Statistics">Office for National Statistics</a> published that Plymouth's unitary authority area population was 256,384;<sup id="cite_ref-ethnicity_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicity-86">[86]</a></sup> 15,664 more people than that of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2001" title="United Kingdom Census 2001">last census</a> from 2001, which indicated that Plymouth had a population of 240,720.<sup id="cite_ref-census_2001_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census_2001-87">[87]</a></sup> The Plymouth <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of urban areas in the United Kingdom">urban area</a> had a population of 260,203 in 2011 (the urban sprawl which extends outside the authority's boundaries). The city's average household size was 2.3 persons.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> At the time of the 2011 UK census, the ethnic composition of Plymouth's population was 96.2% <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">White</a> (of 92.9% was <a href="/wiki/White_British" title="White British">White British</a>), with the largest minority ethnic group being <a href="/wiki/British_Chinese" title="British Chinese">Chinese</a> at 0.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnicity_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicity-86">[86]</a></sup> The white Irish ethnic group saw the largest decline in its share of the population since the 2001 Census (-24%), while the <i>Other Asian</i> and Black African had the largest increases (360% and 351% respectively).<sup id="cite_ref-ethnicity_86-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicity-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> This excludes the two new ethnic groups added to the 2011 census of Gypsy or Irish Traveller and Arab. The population rose rapidly during the second half of the 19th century, but declined by over 1.6% from 1931 to 1951.</p>
<p>Plymouth's <a href="/wiki/Gross_value_added" title="Gross value added">gross value added</a> (a measure of the size of its economy) was 5,169 million <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">GBP</a> in 2013 making up 25% of <a href="/wiki/Devon" title="Devon">Devon</a>'s GVA.<sup id="cite_ref-GVA_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GVA-91">[91]</a></sup> Its GVA per person was £19,943 and compared to the national average of £23,755, was £3,812 lower.<sup id="cite_ref-GVA_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GVA-91">[91]</a></sup> Plymouth's unemployment rate was 7.0% in 2014 which was 2.0 points higher than the South West average and 0.8 points higher than the average for Great Britain (England, Wales and Scotland).<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 2014 profile by the <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service" title="National Health Service">National Health Service</a> showed Plymouth had higher than average levels of poverty and deprivation (26.2% of population among the poorest 20.4% nationally). Life expectancy, at 78.3 years for men and 82.1 for women, was the lowest of any region in the South West of England.<sup id="cite_ref-National_Health_Service_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Health_Service-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
