<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HMNB_Devonport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/HMNB_Devonport.jpg/220px-HMNB_Devonport.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/HMNB_Devonport.jpg/330px-HMNB_Devonport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/HMNB_Devonport.jpg/440px-HMNB_Devonport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HMNB_Devonport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/HMNB_Devonport" title="HMNB Devonport">HMNB Devonport</a> – the largest operational naval base in Western Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-HMNB_Devonport_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HMNB_Devonport-94">[94]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Because of its coastal location, the economy of Plymouth has traditionally been <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/maritime" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:maritime">maritime</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> in particular the defence sector with over 12,000 people employed and approximately 7,500 in the armed forces.<sup id="cite_ref-economy_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy-96">[96]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Gin_Distillery" title="Plymouth Gin Distillery">Plymouth Gin Distillery</a> has been producing <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Gin" title="Plymouth Gin">Plymouth Gin</a> since 1793, which was exported around the world by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gin_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gin-97">[97]</a></sup> During the 1930s, it was the most widely distributed <a href="/wiki/Gin" title="Gin">gin</a> and has a <a href="/wiki/Appellation_d%27origine_contr%C3%B4l%C3%A9e" title="Appellation d'origine contrôlée">controlled term of origin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gin_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gin-97">[97]</a></sup> Since the 1980s, employment in the defence sector has decreased substantially and the public sector is now prominent particularly in administration, health, education, medicine and engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-economy_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/HMNB_Devonport" title="HMNB Devonport">Devonport Dockyard</a> is the UK's only naval base that refits nuclear submarines and the Navy estimates that the Dockyard generates about 10% of Plymouth's income.<sup id="cite_ref-HMNB_Devonport_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HMNB_Devonport-94">[94]</a></sup> Plymouth has the largest cluster of marine and maritime businesses in the south west with 270 firms operating within the sector.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Other substantial employers include <a href="/wiki/University_of_Plymouth" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Plymouth">the university</a> with almost 3,000 staff,<sup id="cite_ref-uni_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uni-76">[76]</a></sup> the national retail chain <a href="/wiki/The_Range_(retailer)" title="The Range (retailer)">The Range</a> at their <a href="/wiki/Estover,_Plymouth" title="Estover, Plymouth">Estover</a> headquarters, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Science_Park" title="Plymouth Science Park">Plymouth Science Park</a> employing 500 people in 50 companies.<sup id="cite_ref-economy_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>Plymouth has a post-war shopping area in the city centre with substantial pedestrianisation.<sup id="cite_ref-gillredev_39-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gillredev-39">[39]</a></sup> At the west end of the zone inside a grade II <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed building</a> is the Pannier Market that was completed in 1959 – <i><a href="/wiki/Pannier" title="Pannier">pannier</a></i> meaning "basket" from French, so it translates as "basket market".<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> In terms of retail floorspace, Plymouth is ranked in the top five in the <a href="/wiki/South_West_England" title="South West England">South West</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> and 29th nationally.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> Plymouth was one of the first ten British cities to trial the new <a href="/wiki/Business_improvement_district" title="Business improvement district">Business Improvement District</a> initiative.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tinside_Pool" title="Tinside Pool">Tinside Pool</a> is situated at the foot of the Hoe and became a grade II listed building in 1998 before being restored to its 1930s look for £3.4&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plymouth_2020">Plymouth 2020</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Plymouth 2020">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small><i>(February 2017)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Since 2003, Plymouth Council has been undertaking a project of urban redevelopment called the "Vision for Plymouth" launched by the architect <a href="/wiki/David_Mackay_(architect)" title="David Mackay (architect)">David Mackay</a> and backed by both Plymouth City Council and the Plymouth Chamber of Commerce (PCC).<sup id="cite_ref-vision_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vision-62">[62]</a></sup> Its projects range from shopping centres, a cruise terminal, a boulevard and to increase the population to 300,000 and build 33,000 dwellings.<sup id="cite_ref-vision_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vision-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Drake_circus_interior.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Drake_circus_interior.jpg/220px-Drake_circus_interior.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Drake_circus_interior.jpg/330px-Drake_circus_interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Drake_circus_interior.jpg/440px-Drake_circus_interior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Drake_circus_interior.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Interior of the <a href="/wiki/Drake_Circus_Shopping_Centre" title="Drake Circus Shopping Centre">Drake Circus Shopping Centre</a> in 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2004 the old Drake Circus shopping centre and Charles Cross car park were demolished and replaced by the latest <a href="/wiki/Drake_Circus_Shopping_Centre" title="Drake Circus Shopping Centre">Drake Circus Shopping Centre</a>, which opened in October 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-dccontroversy_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dccontroversy-104">[104]</a></sup> It received negative feedback before opening when David Mackay said it was already "ten years out of date".<sup id="cite_ref-dccontroversy_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dccontroversy-104">[104]</a></sup> In contrast, the <a href="/wiki/Theatre_Royal,_Plymouth" title="Theatre Royal, Plymouth">Theatre Royal</a>'s production and education centre, TR2, which was built on wasteland at <a href="/wiki/Cattedown" title="Cattedown">Cattedown</a>, was a runner-up for the RIBA <a href="/wiki/Stirling_Prize" title="Stirling Prize">Stirling Prize</a> for Architecture in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is a project involving the future relocation of Plymouth City Council's headquarters, the civic centre, to the current location of the Bretonside bus station; it would involve both the bus station and civic centre being demolished and a rebuilt together at the location with the land from the civic centre being sold off.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Other suggestions include the demolition of the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Pavilions" title="Plymouth Pavilions">Plymouth Pavilions</a> <a href="/wiki/Arena" title="Arena">entertainment arena</a> to create a canal "boulevard" linking <a href="/wiki/Millbay" title="Millbay">Millbay</a> to the city centre. Millbay is being regenerated with mixed residential, retail and office space alongside the ferry port.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Albert_and_Tamar_Bridge_from_Cornwall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Royal_Albert_and_Tamar_Bridge_from_Cornwall.jpg/220px-Royal_Albert_and_Tamar_Bridge_from_Cornwall.jpg" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Royal_Albert_and_Tamar_Bridge_from_Cornwall.jpg/330px-Royal_Albert_and_Tamar_Bridge_from_Cornwall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Royal_Albert_and_Tamar_Bridge_from_Cornwall.jpg/440px-Royal_Albert_and_Tamar_Bridge_from_Cornwall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="1072" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Albert_and_Tamar_Bridge_from_Cornwall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Bridge" title="Royal Albert Bridge">Royal Albert Bridge</a>, 1859 (closest), and <a href="/wiki/Tamar_Bridge" title="Tamar Bridge">Tamar Bridge</a>, 1961 (behind), connect <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a> with Plymouth<sup id="cite_ref-tamar_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tamar-55">[55]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Railways_in_Plymouth" title="Railways in Plymouth">Railways in Plymouth</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/A38_road" title="A38 road">A38 dual-carriageway</a> runs from east to west across the north of the city. Within the city it is designated as 'The <a href="/wiki/Parkway" title="Parkway">Parkway</a>' and represents the boundary between the urban parts of the city and the generally more recent suburban areas. Heading east, it connects Plymouth to the <a href="/wiki/M5_motorway" title="M5 motorway">M5 motorway</a> about 40 miles (65&#160;km) away near <a href="/wiki/Exeter" title="Exeter">Exeter</a>; and heading west it connects Cornwall and Devon via the <a href="/wiki/Tamar_Bridge" title="Tamar Bridge">Tamar Bridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-os_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-os-108">[108]</a></sup> Regular bus services are provided by <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Citybus" title="Plymouth Citybus">Plymouth Citybus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_South_West" title="Stagecoach South West">Stagecoach South West</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Target_Travel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Target Travel (page does not exist)">Target Travel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> There are three <a href="/wiki/Park_and_ride" title="Park and ride">Park and ride</a> services located at <a href="/wiki/Milehouse" title="Milehouse">Milehouse</a>, Coypool (<a href="/wiki/Plympton" title="Plympton">Plympton</a>) and George Junction (<a href="/wiki/Plymouth_City_Airport" title="Plymouth City Airport">Plymouth City Airport</a>), which are operated by Stagecoach South West.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pont_Aven_at_Millbay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Pont_Aven_at_Millbay.jpg/220px-Pont_Aven_at_Millbay.jpg" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Pont_Aven_at_Millbay.jpg/330px-Pont_Aven_at_Millbay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Pont_Aven_at_Millbay.jpg/440px-Pont_Aven_at_Millbay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="928" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pont_Aven_at_Millbay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
MV <i>Pont-Aven</i>: Brittany Ferries service to Roscoff, France and Santander, Spain in Millbay Docks</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A regular international ferry service provided by <a href="/wiki/Brittany_Ferries" title="Brittany Ferries">Brittany Ferries</a> operates from <a href="/wiki/Millbay" title="Millbay">Millbay</a> taking cars and foot passengers directly to France (<a href="/wiki/Roscoff" title="Roscoff">Roscoff</a>) and Spain (<a href="/wiki/Santander,_Cantabria" class="mw-redirect" title="Santander, Cantabria">Santander</a>) on the three ferries, <i><a href="/wiki/MV_Armorique" title="MV Armorique">MV Armorique</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/MV_Bretagne" title="MV Bretagne">MV Bretagne</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/MV_Pont-Aven" title="MV Pont-Aven">MV Pont-Aven</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cremyll_Ferry" title="Cremyll Ferry">Cremyll Ferry</a> is a passenger ferry between <a href="/wiki/Stonehouse,_Plymouth" title="Stonehouse, Plymouth">Stonehouse</a> and the Cornish hamlet of <a href="/wiki/Cremyll" title="Cremyll">Cremyll</a>, which is believed to have operated continuously since 1204.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> There is also a pedestrian ferry from the <a href="/wiki/Mayflower_Steps" title="Mayflower Steps">Mayflower Steps</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mount_Batten" title="Mount Batten">Mount Batten</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> and an alternative to using the <a href="/wiki/Tamar_Bridge" title="Tamar Bridge">Tamar Bridge</a> via the <a href="/wiki/Torpoint_Ferry" title="Torpoint Ferry">Torpoint Ferry</a> (vehicle and pedestrian) across the <a href="/wiki/River_Tamar" title="River Tamar">River Tamar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city's airport was <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_City_Airport" title="Plymouth City Airport">Plymouth City Airport</a> about 4 miles (6&#160;km) north of the city centre.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> The airport was home to the local airline <a href="/wiki/Air_Southwest" title="Air Southwest">Air Southwest</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> which operated flights across the United Kingdom and Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> In June 2003, a report by the <a href="/wiki/South_West_of_England_Regional_Development_Agency" title="South West of England Regional Development Agency">South West RDA</a> was published looking at the future of aviation in the south-west and the possible closure of airports.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> It concluded that the best option for the south-west was to close Plymouth City Airport and expand <a href="/wiki/Exeter_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter International Airport">Exeter International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newquay_Cornwall_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Newquay Cornwall Airport">Newquay Cornwall Airport</a>, although it did conclude that this was not the best option for Plymouth.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> In April 2011, it was announced that the airport would close,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> which it did on 23 December. FlyPlymouth has put forward plans to reopen the city airport by 2018, which would provide daily services to various destinations including <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Plymouth_railway_station" title="Plymouth railway station">Plymouth railway station</a>, which opened in 1877,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> is managed by <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Railway_(train_operating_company)" title="Great Western Railway (train operating company)">Great Western Railway</a> and also sees trains on the <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> network.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Smaller stations are served by local trains on the <a href="/wiki/Tamar_Valley_Line" title="Tamar Valley Line">Tamar Valley Line</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cornish_Main_Line" title="Cornish Main Line">Cornish Main Line</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/First_Great_Western" class="mw-redirect" title="First Great Western">First Great Western</a> have come under fire recently, due to widespread rail service cuts across the south-west, which affect Plymouth greatly.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Three <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">MPs</a> from the three main political parties in the region have lobbied that the train services are vital to its economy.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is a proposal to reopen the <a href="/wiki/Exeter_to_Plymouth_railway_of_the_LSWR" title="Exeter to Plymouth railway of the LSWR">Exeter to Plymouth railway of the LSWR</a> which would connect <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a> and Plymouth to the rest of the UK railway system on an all weather basis. There are proposals to reopen the line from Tavistock to Bere Alston for a through service to Plymouth.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> On the night of 4 February 2014, amid high winds and extremely rough seas, part of the <a href="/wiki/South_Devon_Railway_sea_wall" title="South Devon Railway sea wall">sea wall</a> at Dawlish was breached washing away around 40 metres (130&#160;ft) of the wall and the ballast under the railway immediately behind. The line was closed. <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a> began repair work<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> and the line reopened on 4 April 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> In the wake of widespread disruption caused by damage to the mainline track at <a href="/wiki/Dawlish" title="Dawlish">Dawlish</a> by coastal storms in February 2014, <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a> are considering reopening the Tavistock to Okehampton and Exeter section of the line as an alternative to the coastal route.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>Plymouth is at the southern end of the 99-mile (159&#160;km) long <a href="/wiki/Devon_Coast_to_Coast_Cycle_Route" title="Devon Coast to Coast Cycle Route">Devon Coast to Coast Cycle Route</a> (<a href="/wiki/National_Cycle_Route" class="mw-redirect" title="National Cycle Route">National Cycle Route</a> 27). The route runs mostly traffic free on off-road sections between Ilfracombe and Plymouth. The route uses former railway lines, though there are some stretches on public roads.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_Church_of_St_Mary_and_St_Boniface.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Cathedral_Church_of_St_Mary_and_St_Boniface.jpg/170px-Cathedral_Church_of_St_Mary_and_St_Boniface.jpg" width="170" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Cathedral_Church_of_St_Mary_and_St_Boniface.jpg/255px-Cathedral_Church_of_St_Mary_and_St_Boniface.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Cathedral_Church_of_St_Mary_and_St_Boniface.jpg/340px-Cathedral_Church_of_St_Mary_and_St_Boniface.jpg 2x" data-file-width="457" data-file-height="640" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_Church_of_St_Mary_and_St_Boniface.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Cathedral" title="Plymouth Cathedral">The Catholic cathedral</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Plymouth has about 150 churches and its Roman Catholic cathedral (1858) is in <a href="/wiki/Stonehouse,_Plymouth" title="Stonehouse, Plymouth">Stonehouse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-worship_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worship-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> The city's oldest church is <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Minster" class="mw-redirect" title="Plymouth Minster">Plymouth Minster</a>, also known as St Andrew's Church, (<a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a>) located at the top of Royal Parade—it is the largest parish church in <a href="/wiki/Devon" title="Devon">Devon</a> and has been a site of gathering since AD&#160;800.<sup id="cite_ref-worship_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worship-132">[132]</a></sup> The city also includes five <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptist</a> churches, over twenty <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Church_of_Great_Britain" title="Methodist Church of Great Britain">Methodist</a> chapels, and thirteen <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> churches.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> In 1831 the first <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Brethren" title="Plymouth Brethren">Brethren</a> assembly in England, a movement of conservative non-denominational Evangelical Christians, was established in the city, so that Brethren are often called Plymouth Brethren, although the movement did not begin locally.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>Plymouth has the first known reference to Jews in the <a href="/wiki/South_West_England" title="South West England">South West</a> from Sir <a href="/wiki/Francis_Drake" title="Francis Drake">Francis Drake</a>'s voyages in 1577 to 1580, as his log mentioned "Moses the Jew" – a man from Plymouth.<sup id="cite_ref-worship_132-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worship-132">[132]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Synagogue" title="Plymouth Synagogue">Plymouth Synagogue</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">Listed Grade II* building</a>, built in 1762 and is the <a href="/wiki/Oldest_synagogues_in_the_world" class="mw-redirect" title="Oldest synagogues in the world">oldest</a> <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Ashkenazi</a> Synagogue in the <a href="/wiki/English_speaking_world" class="mw-redirect" title="English speaking world">English speaking world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> There are also places of worship for Islam, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá'í Faith">Bahá'í</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unitarianism" title="Unitarianism">Unitarianism</a>, Chinese beliefs and <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">Humanism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>58.1% of the population described themselves in the 2011 census return as being at least nominally Christian and 0.8% as Muslim with all other religions represented by less than 0.5% each. The portion of people without a religion is 32.9%; above the national average of 24.7%. 7.1% did not state their religious belief.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Since the 2001 Census, the number of Christians and Jews has decreased (-16% and -7% respectively), while all other religions have increased and non-religious people have almost doubled in number.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Plymouth" title="Culture of Plymouth">Culture of Plymouth</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:New_Palace_Theatre_Plymouth.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/New_Palace_Theatre_Plymouth.jpg/220px-New_Palace_Theatre_Plymouth.jpg" width="220" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/New_Palace_Theatre_Plymouth.jpg/330px-New_Palace_Theatre_Plymouth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/New_Palace_Theatre_Plymouth.jpg/440px-New_Palace_Theatre_Plymouth.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1575" data-file-height="1740" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:New_Palace_Theatre_Plymouth.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/New_Palace_Theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="New Palace Theatre">New Palace Theatre</a> in 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Built in 1815, <a href="/wiki/Union_Street,_Plymouth" title="Union Street, Plymouth">Union Street</a> was at the heart of Plymouth's historical culture.<sup id="cite_ref-union_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-union-140">[140]</a></sup> It became known as <i>the servicemen's playground</i>, as it was where sailors from the Royal Navy would seek entertainment of all kinds.<sup id="cite_ref-union_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-union-140">[140]</a></sup> During the 1930s, there were 30 pubs and it attracted such performers as <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Chaplin" title="Charlie Chaplin">Charlie Chaplin</a> to the <a href="/wiki/New_Palace_Theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="New Palace Theatre">New Palace Theatre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-union_140-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-union-140">[140]</a></sup> It is now the late-night hub of Plymouth's entertainment strip,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> but has a reputation for trouble at closing hours.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Outdoor events and festivals are held including the annual <a href="/wiki/British_Firework_Championships" title="British Firework Championships">British Firework Championships</a> in August, which attracts tens of thousands of people across the waterfront.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> In August 2006 the world record for the most amount of simultaneous fireworks was surpassed, by Roy Lowry of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Plymouth" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Plymouth">University of Plymouth</a>, over <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Sound" title="Plymouth Sound">Plymouth Sound</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> Since 1992 the Music of the Night has been performed in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Citadel,_Plymouth" title="Royal Citadel, Plymouth">Royal Citadel</a> by the <a href="/wiki/29th_Commando_Regiment_Royal_Artillery" title="29th Commando Regiment Royal Artillery">29 Commando Regiment</a> and local performers to raise money for local and military charities.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city's main theatres are the <a href="/wiki/Theatre_Royal,_Plymouth" title="Theatre Royal, Plymouth">Theatre Royal</a> (1,315 capacity),<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> its Drum Theatre (200 capacity),<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> and its production and creative learning centre, The TR2.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Pavilions" title="Plymouth Pavilions">Plymouth Pavilions</a> has multiple uses for the city staging music concerts, basketball matches and stand-up comedy.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> There are also three cinemas: Reel Cinema at Derrys Cross, <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Arts_Centre" title="Plymouth Arts Centre">Plymouth Arts Centre</a> at Looe Street and a <a href="/wiki/Vue_(cinema)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vue (cinema)">Vue cinema</a> at the Barbican Leisure Park.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_City_Museum_and_Art_Gallery" title="Plymouth City Museum and Art Gallery">Plymouth City Museum and Art Gallery</a> is operated by Plymouth City Council allowing free admission – it has six galleries.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Plymouth_Athenaeum" title="The Plymouth Athenaeum">The Plymouth Athenaeum</a>, which includes a local interest library, is a society dedicated to the promotion of learning in the fields of science, technology, literature and art. From 1961 to 2009 it also housed a theatre.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>Plymouth is the regional television centre of <a href="/wiki/BBC_South_West" title="BBC South West">BBC South West</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> A team of journalists are headquartered at Plymouth for the <a href="/wiki/ITV_West_Country" title="ITV West Country">ITV West Country</a> regional station, after a merger with <a href="/wiki/ITV_West" class="mw-redirect" title="ITV West">ITV West</a> forced <a href="/wiki/ITV_Westcountry" title="ITV Westcountry">ITV Westcountry</a> to close on 16 February 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> The main local newspapers serving Plymouth are <i><a href="/wiki/The_Herald_(Plymouth)" title="The Herald (Plymouth)">The Herald</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Western_Morning_News" title="Western Morning News">Western Morning News</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/Radio_Plymouth" title="Radio Plymouth">Radio Plymouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Devon" title="BBC Radio Devon">BBC Radio Devon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heart_South_West" title="Heart South West">Heart South West</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pirate_FM" title="Pirate FM">Pirate FM</a> being the local radio stations with the most listeners.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Plymouth" title="Sport in Plymouth">Sport in Plymouth</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Home_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Home_Park.jpg/220px-Home_Park.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Home_Park.jpg/330px-Home_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Home_Park.jpg/440px-Home_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1632" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Home_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Home_Park" title="Home Park">Home Park</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Plymouth is home to <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Argyle_F.C." title="Plymouth Argyle F.C.">Plymouth Argyle F.C.</a>, who play in the third tier of English football league known as <a href="/wiki/Football_League_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League One">Football League One</a>. The team's home ground is called <a href="/wiki/Home_Park" title="Home Park">Home Park</a> and is located in <a href="/wiki/Central_Park,_Plymouth" title="Central Park, Plymouth">Central Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> It links itself with the group of English non-conformists that left Plymouth for the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> in 1620: its nickname is "The Pilgrims".<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> The city also has four <a href="/wiki/Non-League_football" title="Non-League football">Non-League football</a> clubs; <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Parkway_F.C." title="Plymouth Parkway F.C.">Plymouth Parkway F.C.</a> who play at Bolitho Park, <a href="/wiki/Elburton_Villa_F.C." title="Elburton Villa F.C.">Elburton Villa F.C.</a> who play at Haye Road, Vospers Oak Villa F.C. who play at Weston Mill and <a href="/wiki/Plymstock" title="Plymstock">Plymstock</a> United F.C. who play at Deans Cross. All four clubs play in the <a href="/wiki/South_West_Peninsula_League" title="South West Peninsula League">South West Peninsula League</a>.</p>
<p>Other sports clubs include <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Albion_R.F.C." title="Plymouth Albion R.F.C.">Plymouth Albion R.F.C.</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Raiders" title="Plymouth Raiders">Plymouth Raiders</a> basketball club. <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Albion_Rugby_Football_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Plymouth Albion Rugby Football Club">Plymouth Albion Rugby Football Club</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> club that was founded in 1875 and are currently competing in the third tier of Professional English Rugby. They play at <a href="/wiki/The_Brickfields" title="The Brickfields">the Brickfields</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> Plymouth Raiders play in the <a href="/wiki/British_Basketball_League" title="British Basketball League">British Basketball League</a> – the top tier of British basketball. They play at the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Pavilions" title="Plymouth Pavilions">Plymouth Pavilions</a> entertainment arena and were founded in 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_cricket_club" class="mw-redirect" title="Plymouth cricket club">Plymouth cricket club</a> was formed in 1843, the current 1st XI play in the Devon Premier League. <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Devils" title="Plymouth Devils">Plymouth Devils</a> are a <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle_speedway" title="Motorcycle speedway">speedway</a> team in the British <a href="/wiki/National_League_(speedway)" title="National League (speedway)">National League</a>,.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Plymouth was home to an <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> club, the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Admirals" title="Plymouth Admirals">Plymouth Admirals</a> until 2010. Plymouth is also home to Plymouth Marjons Hockey Club, with their 1st XI playing in the National League last season.</p>
<p>Plymouth is an important centre for watersports, especially scuba diving and sailing. The Port of Plymouth Regatta is one of the oldest regattas in the world, and has been held regularly since 1823. In September 2011, Plymouth hosted the <a href="/wiki/America%27s_Cup_World_Series" title="America's Cup World Series">America's Cup World Series</a> for nine days.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_services">Public services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Public services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Devonport_leat_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Devonport_leat_2.jpg/220px-Devonport_leat_2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Devonport_leat_2.jpg/330px-Devonport_leat_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Devonport_leat_2.jpg/440px-Devonport_leat_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Devonport_leat_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Devonport_Leat" title="Devonport Leat">Devonport Leat</a> on <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a> looking up stream</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since 1973 Plymouth has been supplied water by <a href="/wiki/South_West_Water" title="South West Water">South West Water</a>. Prior to the 1973 take over it was supplied by Plymouth County Borough Corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Before the 19th century two <a href="/wiki/Leat" title="Leat">leats</a> were built in order to provide drinking water for the town. They carried water from <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a> to Plymouth. A watercourse, known as Plymouth or <a href="/wiki/Drake%27s_Leat" title="Drake's Leat">Drake's Leat</a>, was opened on 24 April 1591 to tap the <a href="/wiki/River_Meavy" title="River Meavy">River Meavy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Devonport_Leat" title="Devonport Leat">Devonport Leat</a> was constructed to carry fresh drinking water to the expanding town of <a href="/wiki/Devonport,_Devon" class="mw-redirect" title="Devonport, Devon">Devonport</a> and its ever-growing dockyard. It was fed by three Dartmoor rivers: The <a href="/wiki/West_Dart_River" title="West Dart River">West Dart</a>, Cowsic and Blackabrook. It seems to have been carrying water since 1797, but it was officially completed in 1801. It was originally designed to carry water to Devonport town, but has since been shortened and now carries water to <a href="/wiki/Burrator_Reservoir" title="Burrator Reservoir">Burrator Reservoir</a>, which feeds most of the water supply of Plymouth.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Burrator Reservoir is located about 5 miles (8&#160;km) north of the city and was constructed in 1898 and expanded in 1928.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plymouth_Crown_and_County_Courts.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Plymouth_Crown_and_County_Courts.jpg/220px-Plymouth_Crown_and_County_Courts.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Plymouth_Crown_and_County_Courts.jpg/330px-Plymouth_Crown_and_County_Courts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Plymouth_Crown_and_County_Courts.jpg/440px-Plymouth_Crown_and_County_Courts.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1296" data-file-height="972" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plymouth_Crown_and_County_Courts.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Plymouth Combined Crown and County Courts</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Plymouth City Council is responsible for waste management throughout the city and <a href="/wiki/South_West_Water" title="South West Water">South West Water</a> is responsible for sewerage.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> Plymouth's electricity is supplied from the <a href="/wiki/National_Grid_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Grid (UK)">National Grid</a> and distributed to Plymouth via <a href="/wiki/Western_Power_Distribution" title="Western Power Distribution">Western Power Distribution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> On the outskirts of <a href="/wiki/Plympton" title="Plympton">Plympton</a> a <a href="/wiki/Combined_cycle" title="Combined cycle">combined cycle</a> gas-powered station, the <a href="/wiki/Langage_Power_Station" title="Langage Power Station">Langage Power Station</a>, which started to produce electricity for Plymouth at the end of 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Courts_Service" title="Her Majesty's Courts Service">Her Majesty's Courts Service</a> provide a <a href="/wiki/Magistrates%27_Court_(England_and_Wales)" class="mw-redirect" title="Magistrates' Court (England and Wales)">Magistrates' Court</a> and a Combined <a href="/wiki/Crown_Court" title="Crown Court">Crown</a> and <a href="/wiki/County_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="County Court">County Court</a> in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> The Plymouth Borough Police, formed in 1836, eventually became part of <a href="/wiki/Devon_and_Cornwall_Constabulary" class="mw-redirect" title="Devon and Cornwall Constabulary">Devon and Cornwall Constabulary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> There are police stations at Charles Cross and Crownhill (the Divisional HQ) and smaller stations at Plympton and Plymstock.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> The city has one of the Devon and Cornwall Area <a href="/wiki/Crown_Prosecution_Service" title="Crown Prosecution Service">Crown Prosecution Service</a> Divisional offices.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> Plymouth has five fire stations located in Camel's Head, <a href="/wiki/Crownhill" title="Crownhill">Crownhill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenbank,_Plymouth" title="Greenbank, Plymouth">Greenbank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plympton" title="Plympton">Plympton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plymstock" title="Plymstock">Plymstock</a> which is part of <a href="/wiki/Devon_and_Somerset_Fire_and_Rescue_Service" title="Devon and Somerset Fire and Rescue Service">Devon and Somerset Fire and Rescue Service</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Royal_National_Lifeboat_Institution" title="Royal National Lifeboat Institution">Royal National Lifeboat Institution</a> have an <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_85_class_lifeboat" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic 85 class lifeboat">Atlantic 85 class lifeboat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Severn_class_lifeboat" class="mw-redirect" title="Severn class lifeboat">Severn class lifeboat</a> stationed at <a href="/wiki/Millbay_Docks" class="mw-redirect" title="Millbay Docks">Millbay Docks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<p>Plymouth is served by Plymouth Hospitals <a href="/wiki/NHS_Trust" class="mw-redirect" title="NHS Trust">NHS Trust</a> and the city's <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service_(England)" title="National Health Service (England)">NHS</a> hospital is <a href="/wiki/Derriford_Hospital" title="Derriford Hospital">Derriford Hospital</a> 4 miles (6&#160;km) north of the city centre. The Royal Eye Infirmary is located at Derriford Hospital.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/South_Western_Ambulance_Service" title="South Western Ambulance Service">South Western Ambulance Service</a> NHS Foundation Trust operates in Plymouth and the rest of the south west; its headquarters are in <a href="/wiki/Exeter" title="Exeter">Exeter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p>The mid-19th century burial ground at <a href="/wiki/Ford_Park_Cemetery" title="Ford Park Cemetery">Ford Park Cemetery</a> was reopened in 2007 by a successful trust and the City council operate two large early 20th century cemeteries at <a href="/wiki/Weston_Mill" class="mw-redirect" title="Weston Mill">Weston Mill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Efford" title="Efford">Efford</a> both with crematoria and chapels. There is also a privately owned cemetery on the outskirts of the city, Drake Memorial Park which does not allow headstones to mark graves, but a brass plaque set into the ground.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks_and_tourist_attractions">Landmarks and tourist attractions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Landmarks and tourist attractions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Foulston%27s_Town_Hall,_Column_and_Library_in_Devonport_in_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/John_Foulston%27s_Town_Hall%2C_Column_and_Library_in_Devonport_in_2008.jpg/220px-John_Foulston%27s_Town_Hall%2C_Column_and_Library_in_Devonport_in_2008.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/John_Foulston%27s_Town_Hall%2C_Column_and_Library_in_Devonport_in_2008.jpg/330px-John_Foulston%27s_Town_Hall%2C_Column_and_Library_in_Devonport_in_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/John_Foulston%27s_Town_Hall%2C_Column_and_Library_in_Devonport_in_2008.jpg/440px-John_Foulston%27s_Town_Hall%2C_Column_and_Library_in_Devonport_in_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2819" data-file-height="1830" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Foulston%27s_Town_Hall,_Column_and_Library_in_Devonport_in_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Grade I listed Town Hall, Column and Library in Devonport</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Elliot_Terrace,_Plymouth_Hoe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Elliot_Terrace%2C_Plymouth_Hoe.jpg/220px-Elliot_Terrace%2C_Plymouth_Hoe.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Elliot_Terrace%2C_Plymouth_Hoe.jpg/330px-Elliot_Terrace%2C_Plymouth_Hoe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Elliot_Terrace%2C_Plymouth_Hoe.jpg/440px-Elliot_Terrace%2C_Plymouth_Hoe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4024" data-file-height="2848" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Elliot_Terrace,_Plymouth_Hoe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Elliot Terrace, Plymouth Hoe</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a> the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Citadel,_Plymouth" title="Royal Citadel, Plymouth">Royal Citadel</a> was built in 1666 on the east end of <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Hoe" title="Plymouth Hoe">Plymouth Hoe</a>, to defend the port from naval attacks, suppress Plymothian Parliamentary leanings and to train the armed forces. Guided tours are available in the summer months.<sup id="cite_ref-citadel_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-citadel-22">[22]</a></sup> Further west is <a href="/wiki/Smeaton%27s_Tower" title="Smeaton's Tower">Smeaton's Tower</a>, which was built in 1759 as a lighthouse on rocks 14 miles (23&#160;km) off shore, but dismantled and the top two thirds rebuilt on the Hoe in 1877.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> It is open to the public and has views over the Plymouth Sound and the city from the lantern room.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> Plymouth has 20 war memorials of which nine are on <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Hoe" title="Plymouth Hoe">The Hoe</a> including: <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Naval_Memorial" title="Plymouth Naval Memorial">Plymouth Naval Memorial</a>, to remember those killed in World Wars I and II, and the <a href="/wiki/Armada_Memorial" title="Armada Memorial">Armada Memorial</a>, to commemorate the defeat of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Armada" title="Spanish Armada">Spanish Armada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
<p>The early port settlement of Plymouth, called "Sutton", approximates to the area now referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Barbican,_Plymouth" title="Barbican, Plymouth">Barbican</a> and has 100 <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed buildings</a> and the largest concentration of <a href="/wiki/Cobblestone" title="Cobblestone">cobbled</a> streets in Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pilgrim_Fathers" class="mw-redirect" title="Pilgrim Fathers">Pilgrim Fathers</a> left for the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> in 1620 near the commemorative <a href="/wiki/Mayflower_Steps" title="Mayflower Steps">Mayflower Steps</a> in Sutton Pool.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> Also on Sutton Pool is the <a href="/wiki/National_Marine_Aquarium,_Plymouth" title="National Marine Aquarium, Plymouth">National Marine Aquarium</a> which displays 400 marine species and includes Britain's deepest aquarium tank.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p>One mile (two kilometres) upstream on the opposite side of the <a href="/wiki/River_Plym" title="River Plym">River Plym</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Saltram_House" title="Saltram House">Saltram estate</a>, which has a <a href="/wiki/Jacobean_architecture" title="Jacobean architecture">Jacobean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgian_architecture" title="Georgian architecture">Georgian</a> mansion.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the northern outskirts of the city, <a href="/wiki/Crownhill_Fort" title="Crownhill Fort">Crownhill Fort</a> is a well restored example of a "<a href="/wiki/Palmerston_forts" class="mw-redirect" title="Palmerston forts">Palmerston's Folly</a>". It is owned by the <a href="/wiki/Landmark_Trust" title="Landmark Trust">Landmark Trust</a> and is open to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup></p>
<p>To the west of the city is <a href="/wiki/Devonport,_Devon" class="mw-redirect" title="Devonport, Devon">Devonport</a>, one of Plymouth's historic quarters. As part of Devonport's millennium regeneration project, the <i>Devonport Heritage Trail</i> has been introduced, complete with over 70 waymarkers outlining the route.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p>Plymouth is often used as a base by visitors to <a href="/wiki/Dartmoor" title="Dartmoor">Dartmoor</a>, the <a href="/wiki/River_Tamar" title="River Tamar">Tamar</a> Valley and the beaches of south-east <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kingsand" title="Kingsand">Kingsand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cawsand" title="Cawsand">Cawsand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whitsand_Bay" title="Whitsand Bay">Whitsand Bay</a> are popular.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Roland Levinsky building, the landmark building of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Plymouth" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Plymouth">University of Plymouth</a>, is located in the city's central quarter. Designed by leading architect <a href="/wiki/Henning_Larsen" title="Henning Larsen">Henning Larsen</a>, the building was opened in 2008 and houses the University's Arts faculty. It has been consistently considered one of the UK's most beautiful university buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plymouth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Plymouth" title="List of people from Plymouth">List of people from Plymouth</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1590_or_later_Marcus_Gheeraerts,_Sir_Francis_Drake_Buckland_Abbey,_Devon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/1590_or_later_Marcus_Gheeraerts%2C_Sir_Francis_Drake_Buckland_Abbey%2C_Devon.jpg/220px-1590_or_later_Marcus_Gheeraerts%2C_Sir_Francis_Drake_Buckland_Abbey%2C_Devon.jpg" width="220" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/1590_or_later_Marcus_Gheeraerts%2C_Sir_Francis_Drake_Buckland_Abbey%2C_Devon.jpg/330px-1590_or_later_Marcus_Gheeraerts%2C_Sir_Francis_Drake_Buckland_Abbey%2C_Devon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/1590_or_later_Marcus_Gheeraerts%2C_Sir_Francis_Drake_Buckland_Abbey%2C_Devon.jpg/440px-1590_or_later_Marcus_Gheeraerts%2C_Sir_Francis_Drake_Buckland_Abbey%2C_Devon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="777" data-file-height="1060" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1590_or_later_Marcus_Gheeraerts,_Sir_Francis_Drake_Buckland_Abbey,_Devon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sir <a href="/wiki/Francis_Drake" title="Francis Drake">Francis Drake</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>People from Plymouth are known as Plymothians or less formally as <a href="/wiki/Janner" title="Janner">Janners</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> Its meaning is described as a person from <a href="/wiki/Devon" title="Devon">Devon</a>, deriving from Cousin Jan (the <a href="/wiki/Devon" title="Devon">Devon</a> form of <a href="/wiki/John_(first_name)" class="mw-redirect" title="John (first name)">John</a>), but more particularly in <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">naval</a> circles anyone from the Plymouth area.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Elizabethan navigator, Sir <a href="/wiki/Francis_Drake" title="Francis Drake">Francis Drake</a> was born in the nearby town of <a href="/wiki/Tavistock,_Devon" class="mw-redirect" title="Tavistock, Devon">Tavistock</a> and was the mayor of Plymouth.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> He was the first <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">Englishman</a> to circumnavigate the world and was known by the Spanish as <i>El Draco</i> meaning "The Dragon" after he raided many of their ships.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> He died of <a href="/wiki/Dysentery" title="Dysentery">dysentery</a> in 1596 off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> In 2002 a mission to recover his body and bring it to Plymouth was allowed by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">Ministry of Defence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> His cousin and contemporary <a href="/wiki/John_Hawkins_(naval_commander)" title="John Hawkins (naval commander)">John Hawkins</a> was a Plymouth man. Painter Sir <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Reynolds" title="Joshua Reynolds">Joshua Reynolds</a>, founder and first president of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Academy">Royal Academy</a> was born and educated in nearby <a href="/wiki/Plympton" title="Plympton">Plympton</a>, now part of Plymouth. <a href="/wiki/William_Cookworthy" title="William Cookworthy">William Cookworthy</a> born in <a href="/wiki/Kingsbridge" title="Kingsbridge">Kingsbridge</a> set up his successful <a href="/wiki/Porcelain" title="Porcelain">porcelain</a> business in the city and was a close friend of <a href="/wiki/John_Smeaton" title="John Smeaton">John Smeaton</a> designer of the <a href="/wiki/Eddystone_Lighthouse" title="Eddystone Lighthouse">Eddystone Lighthouse</a>. On 26 January 1786, <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Robert_Haydon" class="mw-redirect" title="Benjamin Robert Haydon">Benjamin Robert Haydon</a>, an English painter who specialised in grand historical pictures, was born here. The naturalist Dr <a href="/wiki/William_Elford_Leach" title="William Elford Leach">William Elford Leach</a> FRS, who did much to pave the way in Britain for <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a>, was born at Hoe Gate in 1791.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Antarctic" title="Antarctic">Antarctic</a> explorers <a href="/wiki/Robert_Falcon_Scott" title="Robert Falcon Scott">Robert Falcon Scott</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frank_Bickerton" title="Frank Bickerton">Frank Bickerton</a> both lived in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> Artists include <a href="/wiki/Beryl_Cook" title="Beryl Cook">Beryl Cook</a> whose paintings depict the culture of Plymouth<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Lenkiewicz" title="Robert Lenkiewicz">Robert Lenkiewicz</a>, whose paintings investigated themes of <a href="/wiki/Vagrancy_(people)" title="Vagrancy (people)">vagrancy</a>, sexual behaviour and suicide, lived in the city from the 1960s until his death in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> Illustrator and creator of children's series <a href="/wiki/Mr_Benn" title="Mr Benn">Mr Benn</a> and <a href="/wiki/King_Rollo" title="King Rollo">King Rollo</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_McKee" title="David McKee">David McKee</a>, was born and brought up in South Devon and trained at <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_College_of_Art" title="Plymouth College of Art">Plymouth College of Art</a>. Jazz musician <a href="/wiki/John_Surman" title="John Surman">John Surman</a>, born in nearby <a href="/wiki/Tavistock,_Devon" class="mw-redirect" title="Tavistock, Devon">Tavistock</a>, has close connections to the area, evidenced by his 2012 album <a href="/wiki/Saltash_Bells" title="Saltash Bells">Saltash Bells</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Avant_garde" class="mw-redirect" title="Avant garde">avant garde</a> <a href="/wiki/Prepared_guitar" title="Prepared guitar">prepared guitarist</a> <a href="/wiki/Keith_Rowe" title="Keith Rowe">Keith Rowe</a> was born in the city before establishing the jazz <a href="/wiki/Free_improvisation" title="Free improvisation">free improvisation</a> band <a href="/wiki/AMM_(group)" title="AMM (group)">AMM</a> in London in 1965 and <a href="/wiki/M.I.M.E.O." title="M.I.M.E.O.">MIMEO</a> in 1997. The musician and film director <a href="/wiki/Cosmo_Jarvis" title="Cosmo Jarvis">Cosmo Jarvis</a> has lived in several towns in South Devon and has filmed videos in and around Plymouth.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> In addition, actors Sir <a href="/wiki/Donald_Sinden" title="Donald Sinden">Donald Sinden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Judi_Trott" title="Judi Trott">Judi Trott</a>. George Passmore of <a href="/wiki/Turner_Prize" title="Turner Prize">Turner Prize</a> winning duo <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_and_George" class="mw-redirect" title="Gilbert and George">Gilbert and George</a> was born in the city, as was Labour politician <a href="/wiki/Michael_Foot" title="Michael Foot">Michael Foot</a> whose family reside at nearby <a href="/wiki/Trematon_Castle" title="Trematon Castle">Trematon Castle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup></p>
<p>Notable athletes include swimmer <a href="/wiki/Sharron_Davies" title="Sharron Davies">Sharron Davies</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> diver <a href="/wiki/Tom_Daley_(diver)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tom Daley (diver)">Tom Daley</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> dancer <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Sleep" title="Wayne Sleep">Wayne Sleep</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> and footballer <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Francis" title="Trevor Francis">Trevor Francis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> Other past residents include composer journalist and newspaper editor <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Wills_(journalist)" title="William Henry Wills (journalist)">William Henry Wills</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ron_Goodwin" title="Ron Goodwin">Ron Goodwin</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> and journalist <a href="/wiki/Angela_Rippon" title="Angela Rippon">Angela Rippon</a> and comedian <a href="/wiki/Dawn_French" title="Dawn French">Dawn French</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> Canadian politician and legal scholar <a href="/wiki/Chris_Axworthy" title="Chris Axworthy">Chris Axworthy</a> hails from Plymouth. America based actor <a href="/wiki/Donald_Moffat" title="Donald Moffat">Donald Moffat</a>, whose roles include American Vice President <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a> in the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Right_Stuff_(film)" title="The Right Stuff (film)">The Right Stuff</a></i>, and fictional President Bennett in <i><a href="/wiki/Clear_and_Present_Danger_(film)" title="Clear and Present Danger (film)">Clear and Present Danger</a></i>, was born in Plymouth.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cambridge spy Guy Burgess was born at 2 Albemarle Villas, Stoke whilst his father was a serving Royal Navy officer.</p>
